“# Penman-Monteith Single Method Verification “

]

}, {

“cell_type”: “raw”, “metadata”: {}, “source”: [

“# The purpose of this notebook is to verify that SHyFT implementation of Full Penman-Monteith (FPM) n”, “# and Standardized Penman-Monteith (SPM) equations match reference data provided in ASCE-EWRI, Appendix C.n”, “# ref.: The ASCE Standardized Reference Evapotranspiration Equation, n”, “# Environmental and Water Resources Institute (EWRI) of the American Society of Civil Engineers Task Committee n”, “# on Standardization of Reference Evapotranspiration Calculation, ASCE, Washington, DC, 2005”

]

}, {

“cell_type”: “raw”, “metadata”: {}, “source”: [

“# First we will import all necessary content”

]

}, {

“cell_type”: “code”, “execution_count”: 3, “metadata”: {}, “outputs”: [], “source”: [

“import osn”, “import sysn”, “import mathn”, “from matplotlib import pyplot as pltn”, “from datetime import datetimen”, “from shyft import apin”, “from shyft.time_series import (Calendar,deltahours,UtcPeriod,TimeSeries,TimeAxis,DoubleVector,point_interpretation_policy)”

]

}, {

“cell_type”: “raw”, “metadata”: {}, “source”: [

“# The ASCE-EWRI Appendix C provides verification reference data for n”, “# daily time steps: 10 days in July, 2000.n”, “# hourly time steps: 31-hour period from 16.00 on July 1 to 22.00 on July 2, 2000n”, “# Station: Greeley, Coloradon”, “# Latitude: 40.41 degrees N,n”, “# Longitude: 104.78 degrees W,n”, “# Elevation: 1462.4 m,n”, “# Anemometer height: 3 m,n”, “# Height of temperature/RH meas.: 1.68 m,n”, “# Type of surface: irrigated grass,n”, “# Height veg.: 0.12 m (short crop) or 0.5 (tall crop)”

]

}, {

“cell_type”: “markdown”, “metadata”: {}, “source”: [

“## 24-hour time-step”

]

}, {

“cell_type”: “code”, “execution_count”: 4, “metadata”: {}, “outputs”: [], “source”: [

“utc = Calendar() # provides shyft build-in functionality for date/time handlingn”, “# Single method test based on ASCE-EWRI Appendix C, daily time-stepn”, “# Station data: Greeley, Coloradon”, “# Location:n”, “latitude = 40.41n”, “longitude = 104.78n”, “elevation = 1462.4n”, “# Height of measurementsn”, “height_ws = 3 # height of anemometern”, “height_t = 1.68 # height of air temperature and rhumidity measurementsn”, “# Vegetation infon”, “surface_type = "irrigated grass"n”, “height_veg = 0.12 #vegetation height, short cropn”, “# height_veg = 0.5 #vegetation height, tall cropn”, “# values for stomatal resistance were recalculated based on the info about bulk surface resistances and n”, “# equations B.3-B.6n”, “rl = 100.8 #stomatal resistance, short cropn”, “if height_veg>0.12:n”, ” rl = 100.35 # tall cropn”, “# Some calculated parameters from referencen”, “atm_pres_mean = 85.17 #[kPa]n”, “psychrom_const = 0.0566n”, “windspeed_adj = 0.921n”, “# Data for radiation model, which can be also added into calculations, so there is an option to run either with n”, “# measured radiation or with simulated onen”, “lat_rad = latitude*math.pi/180n”, “slope_deg = 0.0n”, “aspect_deg = 0.0”

]

}, {

“cell_type”: “raw”, “metadata”: {}, “source”: [

“# Let’s create TimeAxis first (I assume that user already familiarizes himself with shyft timeseries concepts)”

]

}, {

“cell_type”: “code”, “execution_count”: 5, “metadata”: {}, “outputs”: [], “source”: [

“n = 10 # nr of time steps: 1 year, daily datan”, “t_start = utc.time(2000, 7, 1) # starting point: 1-07-2000n”, “t_end = utc.time(2000, 7, 10, 23,0,0,0) # end point: 10-07-2000n”, “dtdays = deltahours(24) # returns daily timestep in secondsn”, “n”, “# First, we need a time axis, which is defined by a starting time, a time step and the number of time steps.n”, “tadays = TimeAxis(t_start, dtdays, n) # daysn”, “period = UtcPeriod(t_start,t_end)n”, “# print(len(tadays))”

]

}, {

“cell_type”: “raw”, “metadata”: {}, “source”: [

“# The reference provides the following weather data:”

]

}, {

“cell_type”: “code”, “execution_count”: 6, “metadata”: {}, “outputs”: [], “source”: [

“# Data from weather stationn”, “ws_Tmax = [32.4, 33.6, 32.6, 33.8, 32.7, 36.3, 35.5, 34.4, 32.7, 32.7] # Max air temperature, [degC]n”, “ws_Tmin = [10.9, 12.2, 14.8, 11.8, 15.9, 15.8, 16.7, 18.3, 15.1, 15.7] # Min air temperature, [degC]n”, “ws_ea = [1.27, 1.19, 1.40, 1.18, 1.59, 1.58, 1.13, 1.38, 1.38, 1.59] # actual vapor pressure, [kPa]n”, “ws_Rs = [22.4, 26.8, 23.3, 29.0, 27.9, 29.2, 23.2, 22.1, 26.5, 27.7] # Incoming shortwave radiation, [Mj/m^2/day]n”, “ws_windspeed = [1.94, 2.14, 2.06, 1.97, 2.98, 2.37, 2.43, 1.95, 1.75, 2.31] # Windspeed, [m/s]n”, “n”, “# Results from reference:n”, “ET_os_daily = [5.71, 6.71, 5.98, 6.86, 7.03, 7.50, 7.03, 6.16, 6.20, 6.61] # short crop evapotranspirationn”, “ET_rs_daily = [7.34, 8.68, 7.65, 8.73, 9.07, 9.60, 9.56, 7.99, 7.68, 8.28] # tall crop evapotranspirationn”, “rso_d_ref = [32.43, 32.39, 32.36, 32.32, 32.27, 32.23, 32.18, 32.13, 32.08, 32.02] # simulated insolationn”, “rnet_d_ref = [13.31, 15.20, 13.78, 16.19, 16.33, 16.83, 13.15, 13.00, 15.27, 16.15] # net radiation simulatedn”, “n”, “# conversionsn”, “c_MJm2d2Wm2 = 0.086400n”, “c_MJm2h2Wm2 = 0.0036”

]

}, {

“cell_type”: “raw”, “metadata”: {}, “source”: [

“# Our implementation of Penman-Monteith requires Relative Humidity as imput, so we recalculate from weather data:”

]

}, {

“cell_type”: “code”, “execution_count”: 7, “metadata”: {}, “outputs”: [], “source”: [

“#recalculated inputsn”, “ws_Tmean = []n”, “ws_rhmean = []n”, “ws_svp_tmean = []n”, “n”, “for i in range(len(ws_Tmax)):n”, ” ws_Tmean.append((ws_Tmax[i]+ws_Tmin[i])*0.5)n”, “n”, “for i in range(len(ws_Tmax)):n”, ” ws_svp_tmean.append(0.6108 * math.exp(17.27 * ws_Tmean[i] / (ws_Tmean[i] + 237.3)))n”, “n”, “for i in range(len(ws_Tmax)):n”, ” ws_rhmean.append(ws_ea[i]*100/ws_svp_tmean[i])”

]

}, {

“cell_type”: “raw”, “metadata”: {}, “source”: [

“# From the provided data we create Timeseries, which will be used as an input to our method”

]

}, {

“cell_type”: “code”, “execution_count”: 8, “metadata”: {}, “outputs”: [], “source”: [

“# First, we convert the lists to shyft internal vectors of double values:n”, “tempmax_dv = DoubleVector.from_numpy(ws_Tmax)n”, “tempmin_dv = DoubleVector.from_numpy(ws_Tmin)n”, “ea_dv = DoubleVector.from_numpy(ws_ea)n”, “rs_dv = DoubleVector.from_numpy(ws_Rs)n”, “windspeed_dv = DoubleVector.from_numpy(ws_windspeed)n”, “n”, “tempmean_dv = DoubleVector.from_numpy(ws_Tmean)n”, “rhmean_dv = DoubleVector.from_numpy(ws_rhmean)n”, “n”, “# The TimeSeries class has some powerfull funcionality (however, this is not subject of matter in here).n”, “# For this reason, one needs to specify how the input data can be interpreted:n”, “# - as instant point values at the time given (e.g. such as most observed temperatures), orn”, “# - as average value of the period (e.g. such as most observed precipitation)n”, “# This distinction can be specified by passing the respective "point_interpretation_policy",n”, “# provided by the API:n”, “instant = point_interpretation_policy.POINT_INSTANT_VALUEn”, “average = point_interpretation_policy.POINT_AVERAGE_VALUEn”, “n”, “# Finally, we create shyft time-series as follows:n”, “# (Note: This step is not necessarily required to run the single methods.n”, “# We could also just work with the double vector objects and the time axis)n”, “tempmax_ts = TimeSeries(tadays, tempmax_dv, point_fx=instant)n”, “tempmin_ts = TimeSeries(tadays, tempmin_dv, point_fx=instant)n”, “ea_ts = TimeSeries(tadays, ea_dv, point_fx=instant)n”, “rs_ts = TimeSeries(tadays, rs_dv, point_fx=instant)n”, “windspeed_ts = TimeSeries(tadays, windspeed_dv, point_fx=instant)n”, “n”, “#recalculated inputs:n”, “tempmean_ts = TimeSeries(tadays, tempmean_dv, point_fx=instant)n”, “rhmean_ts = TimeSeries(tadays, rhmean_dv, point_fx=instant)”

]

}, {

“cell_type”: “raw”, “metadata”: {}, “source”: [

“# As mentioned above, in this notebook we can also test our new radiation modeln”, “# which actually can provide data for the Penman-Monteith methodsn”, “# So, simoly create Radiation calculator and you’ll be able to call it’s functionality when needed”

]

}, {

“cell_type”: “code”, “execution_count”: 9, “metadata”: {}, “outputs”: [], “source”: [

“land_albedo = 0.26n”, “turbidity = 1.0 # this is a characteristic of how dusty is the air, 1 – is clean, 0 – dustyn”, “radp = api.RadiationParameter(land_albedo,turbidity)n”, “radc = api.RadiationCalculator(radp)n”, “radr =api.RadiationResponse()”

]

}, {

“cell_type”: “raw”, “metadata”: {}, “source”: [

“# We will now create Calculators for FPM and SPM separately”

]

}, {

“cell_type”: “code”, “execution_count”: 10, “metadata”: {}, “outputs”: [], “source”: [

“method_option = True # FPMn”, “pmp=api.PenmanMonteithParameter(height_veg,height_ws,height_t,rl,method_option)n”, “pmc=api.PenmanMonteithCalculator(pmp)n”, “pmr =api.PenmanMonteithResponse()n”, “n”, “method_option = False # SPMn”, “pmpst=api.PenmanMonteithParameter(height_veg,height_ws,height_t,rl,method_option)n”, “pmcst=api.PenmanMonteithCalculator(pmpst)n”, “pmrst =api.PenmanMonteithResponse()”

]

}, {

“cell_type”: “raw”, “metadata”: {}, “source”: [

“# So, let’s start our simulations”

]

}, {

“cell_type”: “code”, “execution_count”: 11, “metadata”: {}, “outputs”: [], “source”: [

“doy = []n”, “day1 = 183n”, “ET_ref_sim_d = []n”, “ET_sim_st_d = []n”, “rso_sim_d = []n”, “# run simulations for 10 daysn”, “for i in range(n):n”, ” # we call the Radiation Calculator methodn”, ” radc.net_radiation_step_asce_st(radr, latitude, tadays.time(i), deltahours(24),slope_deg, aspect_deg, tempmean_ts.v[i], rhmean_ts.v[i], elevation, rs_ts.v[i]/c_MJm2d2Wm2)n”, ” # collect resultsn”, ” rso_sim_d.append(radr.sw_cs_p*c_MJm2d2Wm2)n”, ” # we call the SPM calculator methodn”, ” pmcst.reference_evapotranspiration(pmrst, deltahours(24),rnet_d_ref[i]/c_MJm2d2Wm2*0.0036, tempmax_ts.v[i], tempmin_ts.v[i], rhmean_ts.v[i], elevation,n”, ” windspeed_ts.v[i]) #expected input of routine is MJ/m^2/hourn”, ” # we call the FPM calculator methodn”, ” pmc.reference_evapotranspiration(pmr, deltahours(24),rnet_d_ref[i]/c_MJm2d2Wm2*0.0036, tempmax_ts.v[i], tempmin_ts.v[i], rhmean_ts.v[i], elevation,n”, ” windspeed_ts.v[i])n”, ” # collect resultsn”, ” ET_ref_sim_d.append(pmr.et_ref) # the outut of et-routine now is in mm/h, here convert to mm/dn”, ” ET_sim_st_d.append(pmrst.et_ref*24)n”, ” # just some days controln”, ” doy.append(day1+1)n”, ” day1+=1”

]

}, {

“cell_type”: “raw”, “metadata”: {}, “source”: [

“# So for 24-hour time step we verified that our FPM and SPM results for short crop are matching reference datan”, “#######################################################n”, “# it is noted in the reference:n”, “# ASCE-FPM, "when computed using a daily calculationn”, “# timestep, was the measure against which the other equations were compared. The ASCE-FPM method, n”, “# using resistance parameters as defined in Manual 70 to be functions ofn”, “# vegetation height and computed with a daily timestep, was the method found to perform bestn”, “# against lysimeter measurements in Manual 70."”

]
